I would never come here if your a single woman or from out-of-state. I came to the shop early Saturday morning for an oil change and possible  front brakes. They only had one car in the beys. All of the technicians were leaned up against equipment not working. The customer service guy saw me walk in and an older hispanic guy behind me. He completely ignored me and went straight to the other guy. I waited about 10 minutes listening to them talk in Spanish before I left. I came back about 10 minutes later same scenario different customer. I had my non expired coupon for the oil change at $49.99. The CSR finally called me to the counter. I explained what I wanted. He took down my information and went outside to check my mileage. He came back in and quoted me a price of $138 for the oil change before all of the additional fees. He claimed that my truck took an extra quart of oil that was going to cost me $20 extra, the coupon for that store expired yesterday despite the print and because I was from Nevada an extra charge was added. Totalling everything to about $178 for an oil change. The wait time would be almost 2 hours because the guys are very busy and the rest of the crew hasn't came to work yet. I explained that I have never paid more than $65 for an oil change ever. I was told to go back to Nevada where it's cheaper. Not knowing that I am born and raised here in Long Beach. As you should know they didn't get my service. I got it done at a great price, no additional quart charges (assumptions make fools out of people. I have a small 3.6L engine not the HEMI) and was straight forward in what I needed. I would never reccomend this establishment to single women or out-of-state travelers. They will try to cheat you.</Review>

My frustrations with PPM are outlined as follows:

Poor customer service: Often times PPM does not post photos of inside of apartments, are not able to provide basic information about apartments such as square footage. There is not a direct line to speak with the person who is processing your application for questions. They will answer text messages, but generally only one text every 2-3 hours, and will only answer 1 question even if you ask 3. Overall very inefficient processing of applications.

False Advertising: Apartments that were listed as "available now" we found out may not be ready for move in for 2-3 months. Although a site may be listed as available, 7/7 properties that we requested already had approvals for other tenants to live there.

Generally not flexible: Unwilling to accommodate minor changes in rental agreements like month-month leases, unwilling to schedule showings on weekends. Move in dates listed set in stone, not open to negotiation.

My dad and I ordered through GrubHub for lunch. They delivered my meal on time and with a smile.
The food however is what I'm reviewing.
I ordered a #2, add cream cheese. There was hardly any cream cheese that I paid extra for. There was also no bacon. The avacados were brown and mushy on my sandwich.
My Dad ordered a roast beef sandwich and enjoyed it even though they forgot the Mayo. He also ordered macaroni salad and got potato salad. He said it tasted fine, nothing special.
The bread I had, dutch crust, was fresh and soft.
Personally, I would not order from here again.<//review>

< text>
Your typical neighborhood market formerly known as Hum's Market now Choice Market with a meat counter so you have your choice from ground beef, oxtails, bacon, chicken, turkey wings and etc. Many of the shoppers are local lottery players or neighbors that don't have easy access to a supermarket because Food 4 less is about a mile away. It's fast and convenient but expect to pay a convenience fee on certain grocery items. Service is ok and they can be friendly once they get to know you. Many people like myself come here to purchase lottery tickets. They are open every holiday but if it's slow they will close early. Don't forget just like any store to check the labels and expiration dates. FYI, They do NOT sell alcohol, beer, wine or spirits. Powerball winner sold here!<//text>

< rate>

< review>
As any martial artist or combat sports athlete/veteran will tell you, running is second to none when it comes to cardio and stamina. It is essential to any conditioning regimen and has been so for ages across all martial arts and combat sports. As with any other physical activity, running comes with its fair share of risk for injury.

That being said, I managed to mess up my right foot pretty bad in an attempt to ramp up my running routine too quickly. After doing some research and reaching out to a few podiatrists, I decided to visit Dr. Suzuki's clinic last week. After all, what better foot doctor could there be for a seasoned runner, or someone relatively new to it like myself, than a doctor that actively participates in marathons?

Truth be told, I was a little hesitant at first as I am still unemployed and working odd jobs to make ends meet as a result of the pandemic. However, having previously been a bartender for 20+ years I have a long history of not always taking the best care of my feet. Ultimately it was an investment in my health and continued growth as a martial artist so I was happy to pay for his expertise, insurance or not.

After running the gamut of standard questions and inquiries, (see what I did there?), Dr. Suzuki inspected my foot and explained that it appeared that I sprained the tendons and ligaments near the cuboid bone of my right foot. He explained the importance of proper footwear when running longer distances and instructed me to refrain from any conditioning oriented activities for a few weeks and to put my foot on ice daily.

Additionally, Dr. Suzuki suggested I look into his recommended "go to" shoes and socks as an avid runner, and gave me his email to "pick his brain" if I had any foot or running related questions in the future. He told me that I wouldn't be needing any shots or additonal treatment, and gave me a complimentary mask/sanitizer bundle for my girlfriend and I.

Then with a grin on his face, Dr. Suzuki proceeded to tell me to feel free to make another appointment with him in the future when/if I have a serious foot injury. He then sent me on my way free of charge! Words can't quite express the debt of gratitude I owe to Dr. Suzuki and his staff for their patience and kindness. It is beyond refreshing to find a doctor that is a true healer in a city where a fair amount of people are only in their respective fields for monetary gain.

Thank you Dr. Suzuki! üëäüôè‚ù§< /review>

1622426733347<//date>
<Rate>5<//Rate>< Review>
As any martial artist or combat sports athlete/veteran will tell you, running is second to none when it comes to cardio and stamina. It is essential to any conditioning regimen and has been so for ages across all martial arts and combat sports. As with any other physical activity, running comes with its fair share of risk for injury.

That being said, I managed to mess up my right foot pretty bad in an attempt to ramp up my running routine too quickly. After doing some research and reaching out to a few podiatrists, I decided to visit Dr. Suzuki's clinic last week. After all, what better foot doctor could there be for a seasoned runner, or someone relatively new to it like myself, than a doctor that actively participates in marathons?

Truth be told, I was a little hesitant at first as I am still unemployed and working odd jobs to make ends meet as a result of the pandemic. However, having previously been a bartender for 20+ years I have a long history of not always taking the best care of my feet. Ultimately it was an investment in my health and continued growth as a martial artist so I was happy to pay for his expertise, insurance or not.

After running the gamut of standard questions and inquiries, (see what I did there?), Dr. Suzuki inspected my foot and explained that it appeared that I sprained the tendons and ligaments near the cuboid bone of my right foot. He explained the importance of proper footwear when running longer distances and instructed me to refrain from any conditioning oriented activities for a few weeks and to put my foot on ice daily.

Additionally, Dr. Suzuki suggested I look into his recommended "go to" shoes and socks as an avid runner, and gave me his email to "pick his brain" if I had any foot or running related questions in the future. He told me that I wouldn't be needing any shots or additonal treatment, and gave me a complimentary mask/sanitizer bundle for my girlfriend and I.

Then with a grin on his face, Dr. Suzuki proceeded to tell me to feel free to make another appointment with him in the future when/if I have a serious foot injury. He then sent me on my way free of charge! Words can't quite express the debt of gratitude I owe to Dr. Suzuki and his staff for their patience and kindness. It is beyond refreshing to find a doctor that is a true healer in a city where a fair amount of people are only in their respective fields for monetary gain.

Thank you Dr. Suzuki! üëäüôè‚ù§</Review>

< name>
Tram Nguyen< /name>
<UserId.>111771331898993153190</UserId.><Time>1526272025152</Time>< Rating>
5<//Rating>
<GmapID>0x80dbf366e9ab8ff1:0x3ba8cd56771c9b1a</GmapID><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPGUWyPWnzRsS5xDK1LzvR9ZZTYsiIakJ_h_WND=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /pics>< response>
None< /response>
<Text>My husband and I had hiked Palomar Mountain most of the day so we were super hungry when we got here. We live in San Diego where the Vietnamese food is seriously lacking so I had low expectations coming into this place. I was born and raised in Saigon so I like to think my tastebuds know what Home tastes like. The little Vietnamese lady that worked the register and hustled in the kitchen was the sweetest. You order at the register, pay, and sit. It‚Äôs not a fancy restaurant, just your local Viet diner attached to a grocery store. They bring the food out to you and without asking, also bring you a tall glass of ice water. We all know about the stereotypical rushed, rude service at Asian joints. You will definitely not find that here. I just wanted to hug these people.

At first glance, one would think this spot specializes in banh mi. However, digging into the Yelp reviews I was surprised to see Bun Bo Hue and Bun Rieu mentioned often. My mom makes the best bun rieu so I never order it when I‚Äôm out. Except Momma is across the country in DC and I was desperate for some comfort food.
So I got the Bun Rieu and almost started crying on first bite. The broth was clean and simple, not extra greasy or salty but had the perfect flavor profile of pork, tomato, and seafood. They made sure all the toppings were there, the rieu (eggy minced pork concoction), congealed pork blood, fish cake (which by itself is another level of delicious), fried tofu, all the salad/mint/bean sprout fixings, AND the legit pungent fermented shrimp paste in a plastic container hidden next to the lemon slice. Trust me, mix some of this into the broth and that umami will hit you in the face. The portion is HUGE and unless you‚Äôre really hungry, you could probably split a bowl between two people.

We also ordered the banh cuon, chewy rice crepe with minced pork which traditionally comes with a side of pork cha lua, nem chua, steamed bean sprouts, and cucumber. Make sure you top this with the fish sauce that comes with it. The texture was chewier than I‚Äôm used to but I really enjoyed it.

Lastly, we ordered a chicken banh mi with all the fixings. I asked the lady to add pate which she happily obliged at no charge. The chicken was slightly dry but I did appreciate the large chunks of meat marinated in turmeric and lemongrass (traditionally it‚Äôs shredded and soy flavored). The baguette itself wasn‚Äôt all that great which was a bummer but we did come at a weird time (3:30pm on a Saturday).

In summary, support your local Mom and Pop! They are a sweet, honest business that deserve a chance. This is as authentic as it gets. The noodle soups taste just like home, or a stoop on an alley in Saigon. We saw a few locals eating in and most of them ordered the bun rieu or bun bo hue. They do have some traditional snacks, desserts, and finger foods pre-made next to the register. They do catering as well (based on all the pictures and signs in the place).< /Text></record></dataset><record>
